\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\begin{DoxyVerb}n-d array object for the array API namespace.

See the docstring of :py:obj:`np.ndarray <numpy.ndarray>` for more
information.

This is a wrapper around numpy.ndarray that restricts the usage to only
those things that are required by the array API namespace. Note,
attributes on this object that start with a single underscore are not part
of the API specification and should only be used internally. This object
should not be constructed directly. Rather, use one of the creation
functions, such as asarray().
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{__array__object_8py_source_l00045}{45}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{__array__object_8py_source}{\+\_\+array\+\_\+object.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{classnumpy_1_1array__api_1_1__array__object_1_1Array_a6827154480d94be0a74a1644c5214556}\index{numpy.array\_api.\_array\_object.Array@{numpy.array\_api.\_array\_object.Array}!\_normalize\_two\_args@{\_normalize\_two\_args}}
\index{\_normalize\_two\_args@{\_normalize\_two\_args}!numpy.array\_api.\_array\_object.Array@{numpy.array\_api.\_array\_object.Array}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\_normalize\_two\_args()}{\_normalize\_two\_args()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classnumpy_1_1array__api_1_1__array__object_1_1Array_a6827154480d94be0a74a1644c5214556} 
 Tuple\mbox{[}\mbox{\hyperlink{classnumpy_1_1array__api_1_1__array__object_1_1Array}{Array}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classnumpy_1_1array__api_1_1__array__object_1_1Array}{Array}}\mbox{]} numpy.\+array\+\_\+api.\+\_\+array\+\_\+object.\+Array.\+\_\+normalize\+\_\+two\+\_\+args (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{x1}{, }\item[{}]{x2}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}, {\ttfamily [protected]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Normalize inputs to two arg functions to fix type promotion rules

NumPy deviates from the spec type promotion rules in cases where one
argument is 0-dimensional and the other is not. For example:

>>> import numpy as np
>>> a = np.array([1.0], dtype=np.float32)
>>> b = np.array(1.0, dtype=np.float64)
>>> np.add(a, b) # The spec says this should be float64
array([2.], dtype=float32)

To fix this, we add a dimension to the 0-dimension array before passing it
through. This works because a dimension would be added anyway from
broadcasting, so the resulting shape is the same, but this prevents NumPy
from not promoting the dtype.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Returns a promoted version of a Python scalar appropriate for use with
operations on self.

This may raise an OverflowError in cases where the scalar is an
integer that is too large to fit in a NumPy integer dtype, or
TypeError when the scalar type is incompatible with the dtype of self.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classnumpy_1_1array__api_1_1__array__object_1_1Array_a85bd05e50f51cba03dbc09e488bad84c}\index{numpy.array\_api.\_array\_object.Array@{numpy.array\_api.\_array\_object.Array}!\_validate\_index@{\_validate\_index}}
\index{\_validate\_index@{\_validate\_index}!numpy.array\_api.\_array\_object.Array@{numpy.array\_api.\_array\_object.Array}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\_validate\_index()}{\_validate\_index()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classnumpy_1_1array__api_1_1__array__object_1_1Array_a85bd05e50f51cba03dbc09e488bad84c} 
numpy.\+array\+\_\+api.\+\_\+array\+\_\+object.\+Array.\+\_\+validate\+\_\+index (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{key}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Validate an index according to the array API.

The array API specification only requires a subset of indices that are
supported by NumPy. This function will reject any index that is
allowed by NumPy but not required by the array API specification. We
always raise ``IndexError`` on such indices (the spec does not require
any specific behavior on them, but this makes the NumPy array API
namespace a minimal implementation of the spec). See
https://data-apis.org/array-api/latest/API_specification/indexing.html
for the full list of required indexing behavior

This function raises IndexError if the index ``key`` is invalid. It
only raises ``IndexError`` on indices that are not already rejected by
NumPy, as NumPy will already raise the appropriate error on such
indices. ``shape`` may be None, in which case, only cases that are
independent of the array shape are checked.

The following cases are allowed by NumPy, but not specified by the array
API specification:

- Indices to not include an implicit ellipsis at the end. That is,
  every axis of an array must be explicitly indexed or an ellipsis
  included. This behaviour is sometimes referred to as flat indexing.

- The start and stop of a slice may not be out of bounds. In
  particular, for a slice ``i:j:k`` on an axis of size ``n``, only the
  following are allowed:

  - ``i`` or ``j`` omitted (``None``).
  - ``-n <= i <= max(0, n - 1)``.
  - For ``k > 0`` or ``k`` omitted (``None``), ``-n <= j <= n``.
  - For ``k < 0``, ``-n - 1 <= j <= max(0, n - 1)``.

- Boolean array indices are not allowed as part of a larger tuple
  index.

- Integer array indices are not allowed (with the exception of 0-D
  arrays, which are treated the same as scalars).

Additionally, it should be noted that indices that would return a
scalar in NumPy will return a 0-D array. Array scalars are not allowed
in the specification, only 0-D arrays. This is done in the
``Array._new`` constructor, not this function.
\end{DoxyVerb}
